The tree\\n83:     special-cases things within an app - namely, root nodes and leaf nodes\\n84:     ignore dependencies to other apps.\\n85:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n86: \\n87:     def __init__(self):\\n88:         self.node_map = {}\\n89:         self.nodes = {}\\n90: \\n91:     def add_node(self, key, migration):\\n92:         assert key not in self.node_map\\n93:         node = Node(key)\\n94:         self.node_map[key] = node\\n95:         self.nodes[key] = migration\\n96: \\n97:     def add_dummy_node(self, key, origin, error_message):\\n98:         node = DummyNode(key, origin, error_message)\\n99:         self.node_map[key] = node\\n100:         self.nodes[key] = None\\n101: \\n102:     def add_dependency(self, migration, child, parent, skip_validation=False):\\n103:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n104:         This may create dummy nodes if they don't yet exist. Any\\n128:         dependencies that were referencing them are changed to reference the\\n129:         `replacement` node instead.\\n130:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n131:         # Cast list of replaced keys to set to speed up lookup later.\\n132:         replaced = set(replaced)\\n133:         try:\\n134:             replacement_node = self.node_map[replacement]\\n135:         except KeyError as err:\\n136:             raise NodeNotFoundError(\\n137:                 \\\"Unable to find replacement node %r. Almost. Remove the\\n164:         replacement node `replacement` and remap its child nodes to `replaced`\\n165:         - the list of nodes it would have replaced. Don't remap its parent\\n166:         nodes as they are expected to be correct already.\\n167:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n168:         self.nodes.pop(replacement, None)\\n169:         try:\\n170:             replacement_node = self.node_map.pop(replacement)\\n171:         except KeyError as err:\\n172:             raise NodeNotFoundError(\\n173:                 \\\"Unable to remove replacement node %r. It recursively resolves all replaced migration keys using `_resolve_replaced_migration_keys()` (line 224), then checks whether all replaced migrations are either fully applied or completely unapplied (lines 251-270).\\n\\nThe completeness validation continues with `check_consistent_history()` (line 344) which uses `all_replaced_applied()` (line 372) to recursively verify that all migrations replaced by a squash migration are marked as applied in the database before allowing the squash migration to be used. This ensures data consistency and prevents partial application states.\\n\\n**Exception Handling:**\\nThe `django/db/migrations/exceptions.py` file defines critical exception classes used throughout the squashing process:\\n- `NodeNotFoundError` - Raised when a dependency references a non-existent migration\\n- `CircularDependencyError` - Raised when circular dependencies are detected\\n- `InconsistentMigrationHistory` - Raised when applied migrations have unapplied dependencies\\n\\nTogether, these components form a comprehensive migration squashing compliance system that ensures squashed migrations maintain proper dependency resolution, prevent circular dependencies, and guarantee data consistency through careful validation of replacement status.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
